## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship of a material. Temperature typically affects elastic modulus and flow stress, while strain determines the deformation response through linear or nonlinear constitutive laws.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (temperature-dependent): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elasticity at fixed T)
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (linear modulus variation with temperature)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(c1 * T) (thermally activated softening/stiffening)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (nonlinear strain hardening, Ramberg-Osgood type)
- Power-law with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (combined hardening and thermal effect)
- Johnson-Cook type: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 + c4 * T) (strain hardening with linear thermal term)
- Ludwik hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (linear + power-law hardening)
- Voce saturation hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) (saturating stress-strain curve)
- Voce with temperature: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) * exp(c2 * T) (saturating hardening with thermal softening)
- Polynomial stress-strain: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (polynomial constitutive law)
- Arrhenius thermal factor: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 / T) (thermally activated deformation, creep-like)
- Hyperbolic sine flow: sigma = c0 * T * asinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 / T)) (Garofalo/sinh creep law inverted)
- Linear thermo-elastic: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * T) (elastic stress with thermal strain subtraction)
- Quadratic temperature dependence: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon (quadratic modulus-temperature relation)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal strain offset → stress depends on (epsilon - c*T), representing subtraction of thermal expansion strain from total strain
- Temperature-dependent modulus → multiplicative factor (c0 + c1*T) or (c0 + c1*T + c2*T**2) multiplying strain terms, reflecting modulus variation
- Arrhenius-type thermal activation → exp(c/T) factor indicates thermally activated processes like diffusion or creep
- Strain hardening saturation → (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) structure indicates stress approaching a saturation value at large strains
- Multiplicative decomposition of thermal and mechanical effects → sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T), separable functions for strain hardening and thermal softening
- Melting/softening singularity → factor like (1 - c0*T)**c1 representing loss of strength approaching a critical temperature
- Strain rate sensitivity analog → sinh or asinh functions of strain appearing in high-temperature deformation models
- Elastic-plastic transition → piecewise or smooth transition between linear (c*epsilon) at small strain and power-law (epsilon**c) at large strain
